## Lean vs Coq, and the cost of maintaining both

First, naming: yes — **Rocq is just Coq, rebranded.** 8.20 (what's installed here) still says "Coq"; the name "The Rocq Prover" lands properly in 9.x. Same system, same `.v` files, no decision there.

### What's actually installed vs. what the proof needs

The proof's center of gravity isn't the tactic language — it's the **formal RISC-V ISA model** the binary's bytes get interpreted against. That dominates everything.

| | Coq (installed) | Lean (not installed) |
|---|---|---|
| Prover present? | ✅ 8.20.1, rich pkg set | ❌ need `elan` + toolchain (network is up, so easy) |
| Mature RV ISA model | ✅ **`riscv-coq`** (MIT PLV / bedrock2) — executable monadic semantics + a real program logic. *Not installed, but buildable.* | ⚠️ no canonical one. Options: **(a) hand-write a tiny RV model**, or **(b) export the official Sail RISC-V model via Sail's newer Lean backend** (heavier, less battle-tested) |
| Program logic over `step` | ✅ comes with bedrock2 | ✗ you build it (small, for our subset) |

### How hard is maintaining two parallel proofs?

Break the work into its real pieces:

1. **The spec** (`nibble`, the `decode` state machine, the I/O-region convention) — pure functional definitions. **Porting is ~1:1, trivial.** Stays in sync with near-zero effort.
2. **The binary** — *the same `.bin`* runs on QEMU and is the proof target for both. **Fully shared.**
3. **The ISA model** — completely different artifacts (riscv-coq vs hand/Sail-Lean). **Zero sharing.**
4. **The refinement proof** (machine code computes `decode`) — different tactic languages, different automation (`lia` vs Lean `omega`), different separation-logic infra. Every invariant and symbolic-execution lemma is re-derived. **This is ~85% of the effort and shares nothing.**

So: shared parts ≈ 10–15% (spec + binary); the expensive parts double. **Realistic cost of "both" ≈ 1.8–1.9× single-system**, plus an ongoing *divergence tax*: every time the binary or spec changes, you re-sync two proofs.

The one *genuine* upside of doing both: because the two ISA models are independently sourced, they **cross-validate each other's semantics** — a real trust gain. But that's a steep premium for a scaffolding rung. Your own handoff frames hex0 as "scaffolding, not a real component… debug the methodology." Paying ~2× on the rung whose job is to *shake out the methodology* is the wrong place to spend it.

### My recommendation

**Go Lean-only for the proof** (your preference), and **mirror only the cheap `decode` spec into Coq** if you want a sanity cross-check — never the proof. Save a full second-system replay for *last*, done once, on the seed specifically — that's actually the high-value moment (it's the "connect tiny-seed trust to proof trust at one point" thesis), and it's a well-scoped one-off rather than a parallel burden.

For hex0's Lean ISA model specifically, I'd **hand-write a minimal RV64I (or RV32I) model**, not pull in Sail-export. hex0 needs maybe ~15–25 instructions; a hand-rolled model is small enough to *hand-audit*, which is literally this project's thesis (tiny auditable seed). The big Sail/bedrock-scale models earn their keep later, at the assembler rung and up.

One concrete tradeoff to be honest about: choosing Lean costs you `riscv-coq`'s mature, ready-made program logic. Coq-only would be the *fastest* path to a machine-code proof today — but it's the system you don't want, and for hex0's tiny subset the hand-rolled-Lean gap is modest.

My plan — build in this order so the two proofs share the maximum:

### 🛠️ **Tool result**

```
# sail-riscv-lean Repository Summary

## What It Is
This project translates the official SAIL RISC-V specification into Lean theorem prover code. It covers the full RISC-V ISA and passes Lean type-checkers without errors, though the authors note the Lean backend remains "work-in-progress" and the resulting code is "neither executable nor polished."

## Generation Process
The repository generates automatically from the official Sail model. To build locally:

1. Install OCaml's opam and dependencies (GMP, Z3, pkg-config)
2. Build Sail from source: `git clone https://github.com/rems-project/sail.git` then `opam install . --deps-only` and `dune build --release`
3. Clone the RISC-V model and build with CMake:
```
cmake -S . -B build -DCMAKE_BUILD_TYPE=RelWithDebInfo
cmake --build build/ --target generated_lean_rv64d
```

## Lean Version & Dependencies
The repository includes a `lean-toolchain` file (exact version unspecified in excerpt). The lakefile.toml indicates it uses Lake for dependency management and likely depends on Lean's BitVector library (with polishing work mentioned for the Lean FRO's maintained version).

## Model Size
The generated model is substantial:
- **Lines:** 171,373
- **Definitions:** 4,612
- **Inductive definitions:** 194
- **Abbreviations:** 189
- **Errors/Warnings:** 0

## RV64D Support
The project explicitly supports RV64D (64-bit RISC-V with double-precision floating point), as evidenced by the target name `generated_lean_rv64d` and output directory `model/Lean_RV64D`.

## Using as a Dependency
No explicit instructions provided for using as an external dependency in the excerpt.
```

### 🤖 **Assistant**

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

I've got what I need on both of your messages. Status:

**QEMU — no rebuild needed.** The only thing missing was the `libcapstone.so.4` SONAME, which QEMU links *for disassembly only* (`-d` logging). Execution never calls into capstone, so shimming `.so.5 → .so.4` is correct and inert — and it's now confirmed working (decoded `Hello\n` correctly, clean exit 0). Rebuilding would only matter if you want `-d in_asm` trace logging. I baked the shim into `make run` so it's reproducible. So we can leave QEMU as-is.

**`sail-riscv-lean` assessment.** I fetched the repo. The important caveats from its own README:

- It's the **official Sail RISC-V model auto-translated to Lean** — authoritative, full ISA (RV64D), type-checks cleanly.
- **But: 171,373 lines / 4,612 defs, and explicitly "work-in-progress… neither executable nor polished."**

That "not executable" part is the catch for *our* use. Our refinement proof wants to take 81 concrete instructions and **reduce the step function over them** (`decide`/`#eval`/`simp`-driven symbolic execution). Over a 171k-line BitVec-heavy generated model that won't reduce, every step becomes manual tactic rewriting against generated definitions — and dragging a 171k-line WIP dependency under a *357-byte auditable seed* inverts the whole "tiny auditable base" thesis.

So my recommendation is a **hybrid that makes "both" pay off twice**:

| Side | Primary proof model | Independent cross-check |
|---|---|---|
| **Lean** | hand-rolled minimal RV64I (~20 instrs, executable, auditable) | later: prove our decode/step agrees with **`sail-riscv-lean`** on these 81 instrs |
| **Coq** | `riscv-coq` (mature, has program logic) | (its own audit) |

That way the hand-rolled Lean model — the thing actually in the TCB — gets validated against the *authoritative* Sail model, and the Coq proof independently validates via riscv-coq. You get real cross-validation on both sides, which is the entire reason to pay for "both."

One genuine fork before I commit the Lean effort:

**🔧 tool → AskUserQuestion**
```json
{"questions": [{"question": "How should sail-riscv-lean be used in the Lean development?", "header": "Sail-Lean role", "multiSelect": false, "options": [{"label": "Cross-check over hand-rolled (recommended)", "description": "Hand-rolled minimal RV64I model is the executable primary proof target (small, auditable, in TCB). sail-riscv-lean used later as an independent oracle: prove our decode+step of the 81 instrs agrees with Sail's. Best of both.", "preview": "Primary: hand-rolled (~20 instrs, executable)\nTCB: tiny + auditable\nSail: validates the hand-rolled model\n-> seed thesis intact, authoritative cross-check"}, {"label": "Sail-Lean as the primary model", "description": "Prove directly against the 171k-line generated Sail model. Authoritative full ISA, but 'not executable/WIP': proofs become heavy manual rewriting, big dependency under the seed. Slower, larger TCB-by-reference.", "preview": "Primary: sail-riscv-lean (171k lines)\nNot executable -> manual tactic rewriting\nBig WIP dependency under a 357B seed\nAuthoritative but heavy"}, {"label": "Skip Sail entirely for hex0", "description": "Hand-rolled Lean model only; defer any Sail cross-check to a later rung (assembler). Fastest path, less cross-validation at the seed.", "preview": "Primary: hand-rolled only\nNo Sail at hex0 rung\nFastest; revisit Sail at assembler rung"}]}]}
```

First, the precise spec design (reconciling `HEX0.md` + `hex0.c` + what `core.s` actually does). I'll model decode as a **single well-founded recursion with an explicit High/Low state** — this ports identically to Lean and gives one clean termination argument:

`decide` fails because the *spec* `decodeS` is well-founded recursive — those don't reduce in the kernel. The model side would reduce, but the spec won't. So kernel `decide` isn't viable against `coreSpec`; `native_decide` (which compiles and runs, handling WF recursion) is the route for certification. I'll use it and document the TCB cost. ### 🤖 **Assistant**

You've put your finger on exactly the right distinction. Let me be honest about it.

## Short answer: you're right — the *certification* theorems are essentially testing

`certify_embedded` / `certify_battery` run the binary on **finitely many fixed inputs** and check the output. That is testing. The fact that it's a `Theorem` doesn't change its epistemic content: it covers 14 inputs, says nothing about the 15th. A binary that's correct on these and wrong elsewhere passes it. **No more coverage than the equivalent QEMU test run.**

What it buys over `qemu-system-riscv64` is narrow and worth naming precisely:

| | QEMU test | Certification theorem (T2) |
|---|---|---|
| Coverage | finite inputs | **same** finite inputs — no better |
| Oracle | expected bytes I typed | `coreSpec` (a formal definition) |
| Emulator in the loop | QEMU (~millions of LoC C) | the ~150-line model you can read |
| Output | a checked artifact composable with the spec | yes |

So the only real gains are: the reference is a formal spec rather than hand-typed bytes, and the "emulator" is a tiny auditable object instead of QEMU. Both are minor, and the second just *trades* trust (you drop QEMU but must now trust the model is faithful — which is itself currently justified by… testing the model against QEMU). So at the T2 level you're essentially correct: **it's testing with a formal oracle and a smaller emulator.** It is *not* categorically stronger than QEMU testing.

## What actually beats testing is the *general* theorem (T1), which I haven't finished

The thing that gives a guarantee no amount of emulation can is:

> **∀ input (of any length), running `core` from a well-formed initial state halts with output = `coreSpec input`.**

That's a statement over the *infinite* input space, established by **induction on the loop**, not enumeration. That is the categorical jump — it rules out the wrong-on-the-15th-input binary by proof. It's the entire point of the verified-tower exercise, and it's task #5/#6, still in progress. Everything so far (bare-metal run, model, certification) is scaffolding and confidence-building *toward* that; on its own it's testing-grade.

I was overstating when I called T2 a "formal proof for the binary" without that qualifier. Accurate framing:
- **Bare-metal run + certification** = testing-grade (finite, but with a formal oracle and an auditable emulator).
- **General refinement (T1)** = proof-grade (all inputs). ← the only part that dominates testing, and it's not done yet.

There's also a second, separate place where I'm legitimately relying on testing rather than proof: **is the model faithful to real RISC-V hardware?** That's an empirical claim right now (model output == QEMU output on the battery). The way to make *that* proof-grade instead of test-grade is task #7 — prove the model's decode+step agrees with the authoritative Sail/`riscv-coq` semantics. Until then, "the model = the hardware" is itself testing-backed.

So: your instinct is correct, and it correctly identifies that the valuable, non-testing deliverable is the general theorem. Let me go finish it — that's where the guarantee lives.

Let me push on T1. First the infrastructure — I'll verify the key primitive (symbolically stepping one instruction over a symbolic-register / concrete-code state) actually works ergonomically in Lean, since that determines the whole approach:

**🔧 tool → Write**

The\n    recipe, demonstrated below for `core`'s first instruction `li t0,0`\n    (= `addi x5,x0,0`, bytes 93 02 00 00, word 0x293):\n\n      1. `have hw : fetch32 s = W := by simp only [fetch32, <byte eqs>]; decide`\n      2. `have hd : Rv64i.decode W = <instr> := by decide`\n      3. `simp [step, hw, hd, State.setPc, State.rset, State.rget, ...]`\n\n    This scales to every instruction: each is a closed-word `decide` for decode\n    plus a `simp` for the effect. -/\ntheorem step_li_t0 (s : State)\n    (h0

## Summary

**The goal has two halves; one is fully done, the other is genuinely a proof and is scaffolded.**

✅ **hex0 runs bare-metal on QEMU RISC-V** — `qemu-system-riscv64 -M virt`, no OS, decodes the embedded input to `Hello\n`, byte-for-byte verified, clean poweroff.

✅ **Formal artifacts, mirrored in Lean *and* Coq** (your "both" choice), all building from scratch:
- **Shared `decode` spec** — compute identically across the two systems.
- **Hand-rolled executable RV64I models** — the 12 instruction forms `core` actually uses.
- **Both models execute the *real binary bytes*** and match the spec on a 13-input differential battery (every error class) — and cross-validate against each other and QEMU.
- **Certification theorems** (proved, no `sorry`): the deployed bytes equal `coreSpec` on the embedded input + battery. Coq's is **kernel-checked via `vm_compute`** (smaller TCB); Lean's uses `native_decide`.

🚧 **General refinement (`core_refines`, ∀ inputs)** — scaffolded in both. The **per-step reduction primitive is fully proved** (`step_li_t0`, `Qed`/no-sorry), and the loop invariant + `WellFormed` + theorem statement are pinned down. The inductive loop body is the one remaining `sorry`/`Admitted`, documented in `STATUS.md`.

## The thing your question forced me to be honest about

You were right: items above marked "certification" and the bare-metal run are **testing-grade** — finite inputs, a formal oracle and a tiny auditable emulator instead of QEMU, but no universal coverage. **The only deliverable that dominates testing is `core_refines`** (induction over all inputs), and that's the part still in progress. I've written this plainly into `STATUS.md` and `TCB.md` rather than papering over it.

8 commits, clean repo (34 source files, no build artifacts), `TCB.md` enumerates the trusted base (notably: "model = real hardware" is currently testing-backed — task #7 fixes that via Sail/`riscv-coq` cross-check).

Finishing the general proof in both systems is a substantial, multi-session effort (the loop-body simulation with BitVec↔Nat arithmetic + code/output disjointness framing). How do you want to prioritize?

| Your step | Lean status |

## What's left for `core_refines`

Exactly your step 3 **machine side** + step 4:
- **One-iteration lemma**: from `LoopInv .. rest emitted`, case-split on the head char's class and run the body — spacing→loop, nibble-pair→`sb`+loop, comment→sub-loop, error→halt — landing in `LoopInv .. rest' emitted'` with `rest'.length < rest.length`. This needs the input/output **disjointness frame** for the store and the BitVec↔Nat arithmetic (`nibble = c−48/−55`, `hi*16+lo` via `slli`+`or`). The engine + spec lemmas reduce it to mechanical (but lengthy) case work — the `sb`/comment cases are the meatiest.
- **Induction** on `rest.length` (base = `core_eof`) telescoping `emitted ++ decode rest` into `coreSpec`.

This is the frontier shrinking exactly as you laid out. Everything compiles and is committed (8 commits on the refinement, latest `c22125a`).

Grinding. The right foundation for the induction is a **`runFuel` composition lemma** (`runFuel 0 (a+b) s = runFuel 0 b (runFuel 0 a s)`) and a halt-absorption lemma — these let me chain per-token runs into the full run. Let me prove them:

**🔧 tool → Edit**
```json
{"replace_all": false, "file_path": "/var/data/bootstrap/lean/Hex0/Refine.lean", "old_string": "@[simp] theorem rset_zero (s : State) (v : Word) : s.rset 0 v = s := by\n  unfold State.rset; simp", "new_string": "@[simp] theorem rset_zero (s : State) (v : Word) : s.rset 0 v = s := by\n  unfold State.rset; simp\n\n/-- Once halted (pc = 0), more fuel changes nothing. -/\ntheorem runFuel_halt (b : Nat) (s : State) (h : s.pc = 0) : runFuel 0 b s = s := by\n  cases b with\n  | zero => rfl\n  | succ n => simp [runFuel, h]\n\n/-- Fuel composition: running `a+b` steps = running `b` more after the first `a`.\n    Holds unconditionally (halting is absorbed). The backbone of the induction. -/\ntheorem runFuel_add (a b : Nat) (s : State) :\n    runFuel 0 (a + b) s = runFuel 0 b (runFuel 0 a s) := by\n  induction a generalizing s with\n  | zero => simp [runFuel]\n  | succ a ih =>\n    rw [show a + 1 + b = (a + b) + 1 from by omega]\n    by_cases h : s.pc = 0\n    · simp [runFuel_halt, h]\n    · simp only [runFuel, h, if_false]; rw [ih]"}
```

## Milestone: the induction is proved

Since "keep grinding," here's what got done this stretch — the **mathematically substantive half of `core_refines`**:

**Newly proved (`sorry`-free, kernel-only):**
- **`runFuel_add`** / **`runFuel_halt`** — fuel composition (`runFuel (a+b) = runFuel b ∘ runFuel a`), the backbone for chaining per-token runs.
- **`decodeS_spacing` / `decodeS_byte` / `decodeS_comment_skip`** — your step 3, spec side (`decode(token++rest) = decode token ++ decode rest`).
- **Arithmetic toolkit** — `ult_ofNat` (resolves `bgeu`), `ofNat_ne` (resolves `beq`), `getD_drop` (the input read).
- **`eof_result`** — the EOF case packaged as a `coreSpec`-correct result (via `core_eof` + `spec_link`: at end-of-input `decode inp = (emitted, Ok)`, so `coreSpec = (0, emitted, |emitted|)`).
- **`loop_correct`** — **your step 4, the full induction, PROVED.** Structural induction on a fuel bound on `rest.length`; base = `eof_result`, step = `loop_iteration`, runs chained by `runFuel_add`, spec telescoped by `spec_link`.

So steps **1, 2, 3-spec, and 4 are all proved.** `LoopInv` now also carries `spec_link` (ties machine progress to `decodeS inp`) and `in_mem` (input in memory).

## The 2 remaining `sorry`s — precisely localized

1. **`loop_iteration`** — your step 3 *machine* side: one loop-body iteration. Case-split on the head char (spacing→loop / nibble-pair→`sb`+loop / comment→sub-loop / 3 errors→halt). All the tools exist (engine + arithmetic + spec lemmas); it's lengthy mechanical case work, the `sb`/comment cases being meatiest.
2. **`core_refines`** — the prologue: `initOn → LoopInv inp cap _ inp []` (`loadBytes` correctness + the 2 entry instructions `li t0,0; li t1,0`), then hand off to `loop_correct`.

39 proved declarations in the refinement file; 10 commits on it. Everything builds from scratch.

That's the natural seam: **the whole proof skeleton is assembled and verified except the per-token machine stepping and the entry setup.** I'll keep grinding into `loop_iteration` next (starting with the spacing token to lock the loop-back pattern) — flagging that it's the long mechanical stretch, so it'll land in pieces.

### 🛠️ **Tool result**

```
      = BitVec.ofNat 8 ((Hex0.coreSpec inp cap).2.1.getD j 0)

/-- The shared head of every non-EOF iteration: `bgeu`(not taken) → `add` →
    `lbu` (read input char `c`) → `addi` (bump index). After 4 steps the machine
    is at offset 24 with `t2 = c`, `t0` bumped, memory and other registers intact. -/
set_option maxRecDepth 4000 in
theorem loop_prefix (inp : List Nat) (cap : Nat) (c : Nat) (rest' emitted : List Nat)
    (s : State) (inv : LoopInv inp cap s (c :: rest') emitted) :
    ∃ s4, runFuel 0 4 s = s4 ∧
      s4.pc = BitVec.ofNat 64 (Image.coreAddr + 24) ∧
      s4.rget 7 = BitVec.ofNat 64 c ∧
      s4.rget 5 = s.rget 5 + 1 ∧
      s4.mem = s.mem ∧ CodeLoaded s4 ∧
      (∀ i, i ≠ 5 → i ≠ 7 → i ≠ 28 → s4.rget i = s.rget i) := by
  -- length / value facts about the current index
  have hsuf := inv.suffix
  have hge : (c :: rest').length ≤ inp.length := by
    have h := congrArg List.length hsuf; simp [List.length_drop] at h; omega
  have hilt : inp.length - (c :: rest').length < inp.length := by simp [List.length_cons]; omega
  have hgetd : inp.getD (inp.length - (c :: rest').length) 0 = c := by
    rw [← getD_drop]; rw [hsuf]; rfl
  have hilt64 : inp.length < 2 ^ 64 := by have := inv.in_lt; omega
  have hc256 : c < 256 := by
    apply inv.bytes_lt; have : c ∈ inp.drop (inp.length - (c :: rest').length) := by
      rw [hsuf]; exact List.mem_cons_self _ _
    exact List.drop_subset _ _ this
  have hpc0 : s.pc = BitVec.ofNat 64 (Image.coreAddr + 8) := inv.at_loop.trans (by decide)
  -- step 1: bgeu t0,a1 -- NOT taken (idx < len)
```

## Progress this stretch — `loop_prefix` proved

`loop_iteration`'s machinery now has its cornerstone done:

- **`loop_prefix`** (PROVED, kernel-only) — the shared 4-instruction head of *every* non-EOF iteration: `bgeu`(not-taken) → `add t3,a0,t0` → `lbu t2` (reads the input char `c`) → `addi t0`. After 4 steps: pc at offset 24, `t2 = c`, index bumped, memory and all other registers intact. **This is the piece that includes the `lbu` input-memory read** — the part I flagged as meatiest — with the full framing (`in_mem` + `getD_drop` + `setWidth8_64` zero-extend).
- Supporting lemmas proved along the way: `setWidth8_64`, and `LoopInv` extended with `in_lt`/`bytes_lt`.

**41 proved declarations** in the refinement file; still exactly **2 `sorry`s** (`loop_iteration`, `core_refines`), build green from scratch.

## What `loop_iteration` still needs

From `loop_prefix`'s output state `s4`, the **per-class tail**:
- the `beq` char-dispatch chain (compare `c` against `# ; \n ' ' _` then the nibble ranges),
- then per class: **spacing**→back to loop / **nibble-pair**→`sb`+loop / **comment**→inner skip-loop / **3 errors**→halt,
- rebuilding `LoopInv` for the shorter suffix (using `decodeS_spacing`/`byte`/`comment_skip` for `spec_link`; the `sb` and comment cases carry the output↔code disjointness frame).

All the tools exist now (engine, `loop_prefix`, arithmetic toolkit, spec decomposition). It's mechanical but voluminous — each token class is its own `beq`-chain + `LoopInv` reconstruction (~60–100 lines each), and there are ~6 classes, plus the `core_refines` prologue (`loadBytes` correctness + 2 entry instructions).

### 🤖 **Assistant**

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

Milestone reached. Here's where the proof stands.

## A complete machine-code iteration is now proved

`loop_spacing_nl` : `LoopInv (10::rest') → ∃k, LoopInv rest'` — one **full main-loop iteration**, machine-code level, end-to-end, `sorry`-free. It composes three freshly-proved pieces:

- **`loop_prefix`** — the shared `bgeu`→`add`→`lbu`→`addi` head, *including the `lbu` input-memory read* with full framing.
- **`spacing_tail_nl`** — the `beq` dispatch chain (6 steps) resolving to the loop-back.
- **`spacing_loopinv`** — rebuilding the 16-field invariant for the shorter suffix (idx, suffix, `spec_link` via `decodeS_spacing`).

…and plugs into the already-proven induction (`loop_correct`) via `runFuel_add`.

**This is the key validation:** the entire machine-side architecture composes correctly and connects to the induction. **45 proved declarations**, still just **2 `sorry`s** (`loop_iteration`, `core_refines`), green from scratch.

## What this means for finishing

Every *pattern* needed for `core_refines` is now proved at least once:

| Pattern | Proved by |
|---|---|
| read input char (`lbu` + memory frame) | `loop_prefix` ✓ |
| char dispatch (`beq` chain) + loop-back | `spacing_tail_nl` ✓ |
| invariant rebuild for shorter suffix | `spacing_loopinv` ✓ |
| one complete iteration | `loop_spacing_nl` ✓ |
| the induction over all iterations | `loop_correct` ✓ |
| base case (halt) | `core_eof` ✓ |

The remaining work in `loop_iteration` is **mechanical replication** of these proven patterns:
- spacing `' '` / `'_'` — identical to `nl`, just 2/4 more `beq` steps in the tail;
- **nibble→byte**: same prefix, then parse-two-nibbles + `sb` store (adds the output↔code/input disjointness frame) + invariant rebuild via `decodeS_byte`;
- **comment**: prefix, then an inner skip-loop (its own small induction) + rebuild via `decodeS_comment_skip`;
- **3 error classes**: prefix, then dispatch to an error epilogue → halt (like `core_eof`);
- a `dispatch` on the head char's class, then `core_refines`'s prologue (`loadBytes` correctness + 2 entry instructions).

Each is its own focused pass (~60–150 lines), reusing the proved lemmas. None requires a *new* technique — the hard parts (memory-read framing, branch resolution, invariant telescoping, the induction) are done.

I've been grinding continuously and every step is committed, so this is a clean, resumable state. Given the remaining is several mechanical passes of the now-proven patterns, this is a strong checkpoint — but I'm happy to keep going class-by-class (the **nibble/byte** case is the most interesting next one, since it exercises the `sb` store + disjointness frame). Want me to continue with that, or hold here?

Both nearly work — the `range/getD` needs `getElem?` simp, and the byte case needs a `nibble < 16` fact. Let me nail both:

**🔧 tool → Bash**
```json
{"command": "export PATH=\"$HOME/.elan/bin:$PATH\" && cat > /tmp/conv2.lean <<'EOF'\nimport Hex0.Spec\nopen Hex0\ntheorem nibble_lt (c v : Nat) (h : nibble c = some v) : v < 16 := by\n  unfold nibble at h; split at h <;> simp_all <;> omega\ntheorem range_getD (l : List Nat) : (List.range l.length).map (fun i => l.getD i 0) = l := by\n  apply List.ext_getElem\n  · simp\n  · intro i h1 h2\n    simp only [List.getElem_map, List.getElem_range, List.getD_eq_getElem?_getD]\n    rw [List.getElem?_eq_getElem (by simpa using h1)]; rfl\ntheorem decode_bytes_lt : ∀ (st : St) (l : List Nat) (b : Nat),\n    b ∈ (decodeS st l).1 → b < 256 := by\n  intro st l\n  induction st, l using decodeS.induct with\n  | _ => intro b hb <;> simp_all [decodeS] <;>\n         first\n         | omega\n         | (have h1 := nibble_lt _ _ ‹nibble _ = some _›; omega)\nEOF\nlake env lean /tmp/conv2.lean 2>&1 | grep -vE 'warning|unused|Hint|Note|disabled|̵' | head -20; echo \"EXIT=${PIPESTATUS[0]}\"", "description": "Test helper lemmas v2"}
```

### 🛠️ **Tool result**

## `core_refines` — the entire prologue is now proved

The hard, foundational half is done (all `sorry`-free, kernel-only):
- **`loadBytes_frame` / `loadBytes_get`** — `loadBytes` correctness (I redefined it recursively so it's provable by induction; certs stay green since semantics are identical).
- **`code_initOn` / `in_initOn`** — `initOn` loads code and input correctly, via the `loadBytes` lemmas + region disjointness (code `[coreAddr, inputAddr)` is adjacent-disjoint from input; input fits before output by `WellFormed`).
- **`init_loopinv`** — the prologue: `initOn` → the 2 entry instructions `li t0,0; li t1,0` → the **full 16-field `LoopInv inp cap _ inp []`**.

With `init_loopinv` + the already-proven `loop_correct`, **`core_refines` is reduced to a pure spec↔observation conversion with no machine code left** — just `(ofNat status).toNat = status`, and `readMem … = out` (which needs `(List.range out.length).map (out.getD ·) = out` — verified — plus "decoded bytes `< 256`"). That last lemma (`decodeS_bytes_lt`) is true and almost mechanized; it's fighting me only on threading the `Low hi ⇒ hi<16` precondition through `decodeS.induct`. No deep obstacle — pure list/spec tactic plumbing.

## `loop_iteration` — a complete iteration proved (newline token)

`loop_spacing_nl` = `loop_prefix` (read char) + `spacing_tail_nl` (dispatch) + `spacing_loopinv` (rebuild) is a full machine-code iteration. The remaining classes (other spacing chars, nibble→`sb`, comment→sub-loop, 3 errors) are the same pattern.

The vacuous-precond proof `by cases h` wrongly "succeeds" on `Low=Low` leaving a hole; and the `if false=true` wasn't reduced. Let me use `absurd h (by decide)` (which correctly discriminates `High≠Low` from `Low=Low`) and full `simp_all`:

**🔧 tool → Bash**
```json
{"command": "export PATH=\"$HOME/.elan/bin:$PATH\" && cat > /tmp/conv10.lean <<'EOF'\nimport Hex0.Spec\nopen Hex0\ntheorem nibble_lt (c v : Nat) (h : nibble c = some v) : v < 16 := by\n  unfold nibble at h; split at h <;> simp_all <;> omega\ntheorem decodeS_bytes_lt : ∀ (st : St) (l : List Nat),\n    (∀ hi, st = St.Low hi → hi < 16) → ∀ b ∈ (decodeS st l).1, b < 256 := by\n  intro st l\n  induction st, l using decodeS.induct <;> intro hpre b hb <;>\n    simp_all [decodeS] <;>\n    first\n      | (rename_i ih; exact ih (fun _ h => absurd h (by decide)) b hb)\n      | (rename_i hnib ih; exact ih (nibble_lt _ _ hnib) b hb)\n      | (rcases hb with h | h\n         · subst h\n           have h1 := nibble_lt _ _ (by assumption)\n           have h2 := hpre _ rfl\n           omega\n         · rename_i ih; exact ih (fun _ hh => absurd hh (by decide)) b h)\ntheorem decode_bytes_lt (l : List Nat) : ∀ b ∈ (decode l).1, b < 256 :=\n  decodeS_bytes_lt St.High l (fun _ h => absurd h (by decide))\nEOF\nlake env lean /tmp/conv10.lean 2>&1 | grep -vE 'warning|unused|Hint|Note|disabled|̵' | head -25; echo \"EXIT=${PIPESTATUS[0]}\"", "description": "Test decode_bytes_lt v10"}
```

```json
{"command": "export PATH=\"$HOME/.elan/bin:$PATH\" && cat > /tmp/conv12.lean <<'EOF'\nimport Hex0.Spec\nopen Hex0\ntheorem nibble_lt (c v : Nat) (h : nibble c = some v) : v < 16 := by\n  unfold nibble at h; split at h <;> simp_all <;> omega\ntheorem decodeS_bytes_lt : ∀ (st : St) (l : List Nat),\n    (∀ hi, st = St.Low hi → hi < 16) → ∀ b, b ∈ (decodeS st l).1 → b < 256\n  | .High, [], _, b, hb => by simp [decodeS] at hb\n  | .Low _, [], _, b, hb => by simp [decodeS] at hb\n  | .High, c :: rest, _, b, hb => by\n      rw [decodeS] at hb\n      by_cases hc : isComment c = true\n      · rw [if_pos hc] at hb\n        have hlt := skipComment_len rest\n        exact decodeS_bytes_lt .High (skipComment rest) (fun _ h => nomatch h) b hb\n      · rw [if_neg hc] at hb\n        by_cases hs : isSpace c = true\n        · rw [if_pos hs] at hb\n          exact decodeS_bytes_lt .High rest (fun _ h => nomatch h) b hb\n        · rw [if_neg hs] at hb\n          cases hn : nibble c with\n          | none => rw [hn] at hb; simp [decodeS] at hb\n          | some hi => rw [hn] at hb\n                       exact decodeS_bytes_lt (.Low hi) rest\n                         (fun hi' h => by cases h; exact nibble_lt _ _ hn) b hb\n  | .Low hi, c :: rest, hpre, b, hb => by\n      rw [decodeS] at hb\n      by_cases hls : isLowStop c = true\n      · rw [if_pos hls] at hb; simp at hb\n      · rw [if_neg hls] at hb\n        cases hn : nibble c with\n        | none => rw [hn] at hb; simp at hb\n        | some l
```

## `core_refines` is proved — the general refinement is down to a single `sorry`

```lean
theorem core_refines (inp : List Nat) (cap : Nat) (hwf : WellFormed inp cap) :
    ∃ fuel, Harness.observe inp cap fuel = Hex0.coreSpec inp cap
```

This — **"for every input, the deployed binary's RISC-V execution produces exactly what the spec prescribes"** — now type-checks. The entire verified tower for hex0 is assembled and verified, and the **only** remaining `sorry` is `loop_iteration` (the per-token machine-stepping lemma), of which a **complete instance is already proved** (`loop_spacing_nl`).

### What got proved this turn (all `sorry`-free, kernel-only)

The whole `core_refines` chain:
- **Prologue**: `loadBytes_frame`/`loadBytes_get` (recursive `loadBytes` correctness), `code_initOn`/`in_initOn` (region disjointness), **`init_loopinv`** (`initOn` → 2 entry instrs → full `LoopInv`).
- **Induction**: `loop_correct` (proved earlier) + `runFuel_add`.
- **Conversion** (`observe ↔ coreSpec`, pure spec/arithmetic): `decode_bytes_lt` (all output bytes `< 256`, via explicit well-founded recursion with the `Low hi ⇒ hi<16` precondition), `range_getD`, `coreSpec_props`, and the `toNat`/`ofNat` plumbing.

**55 proved declarations**, **1 `sorry`**, everything green from scratch, 25 commits.

### The single remaining gap

`loop_iteration` — one main-loop iteration. The pattern is **fully demonstrated** by `loop_spacing_nl` (`loop_prefix` reads the char → `spacing_tail_nl` dispatches → `spacing_loopinv` rebuilds). Closing it means replicating that across: the other two spacing chars (analogous), nibble→`sb` (adds the output↔code/input disjointness frame), comment→inner-loop, the 3 error→halt classes, and a head-char dispatch. Mechanical, but voluminous — no new techniques.

### Honest framing

The headline result you asked for — **a formal proof that the bare-metal binary implements the hex0 spec for all inputs** — is *proved modulo one machine-stepping lemma whose pattern is itself proved complete*. That's the difference between "verified" and "verified with one `sorry` whose shape is known to close." Fully discharging `loop_iteration` (zero `sorry`) is a well-scoped continuation: each token class is its own `loop_prefix`+tail+rebuild pass reusing the proved lemmas.

I've pushed this from a bare scaffold to this state across the session and committed every step, so it's cleanly resumable. Want me to keep grinding `loop_iteration`'s remaining classes (next natural target: the **nibble→byte** case, since it's the one exercising the `sb` store + disjointness frame — the last genuinely new piece), or is this single-`sorry`, `core_refines`-proved state a good point to hold?

### 🤖 **Assistant**

Here's where things genuinely stand.

## State: 1 `sorry`, `core_refines` proved, 56 proved declarations

The headline theorem — **for every input, the deployed binary computes the spec** — type-checks. The single remaining `sorry` is `loop_iteration` (one main-loop iteration), and everything that consumes it (`loop_correct`, `core_refines`) is proved against it.

This session I pushed it from `core_refines = sorry` to **`core_refines` fully proved**, by closing the entire conversion (`decode_bytes_lt`, `range_getD`, `coreSpec_props`, the `toNat`/`ofNat`/`readMem` plumbing) and building the prologue. Plus a complete iteration instance (`loop_spacing_nl`) and the reusable `li_beq_ne` block.

## The honest read on "so close"

It *is* close **conceptually** — one lemma, and its pattern is fully proved end-to-end (`loop_prefix` → `beq`-dispatch → `spacing_loopinv` → feeds the induction). But `loop_iteration` is **large in raw proof volume**: it's a dispatch over 6 token classes, each its own machine-stepping chain:

| class | needs | built? |
|---|---|---|
| spacing `\n` | `loop_spacing_nl` | ✅ done |
| spacing `' '`,`'_'` | longer `beq` tails (use `li_beq_ne`) | tooling ready |
| comment | inner skip-loop (own small induction) | — |
| nibble→byte | `blt/bge` parse + **`sb`-store disjointness frame** | the new piece |
| 3 errors | parse-to-fail → halt epilogue | — |
| dispatch | case on `c`, combine | — |

Realistically that's ~400–600 more lines of intricate (if mechanical) Lean — the `sb`-store frame being the one genuinely new technique. I've built the hard reusable pieces (`loop_prefix`, `li_beq_ne`, `spacing_loopinv`, the whole conversion), so it's *assembly of proven patterns*, not new math — but it's not something I can responsibly land in this session's remaining budget without risking a broken build, and partial work on it wouldn't reduce the `sorry` count.

## My recommendation

This is an excellent, coherent stopping point: **bare-metal hex0 running on QEMU RISC-V, dual (Lean+Coq) spec/model/certification all cross-validated, and the general refinement theorem proved in Lean modulo a single, well-understood, pattern-demonstrated lemma.** 30 commits, everything green from scratch.

To finish `loop_iteration` to zero `sorry`, the cleanest path is a focused follow-up that goes class-by-class (I'd start with the `sb`-store frame since it's the only new technique, then the byte case, then mechanically the rest). I can take that on in a fresh pass where I have the budget to do it carefully and keep it building at every step.

## Written for next session

**`/var/data/bootstrap/RESUME.md`** (committed) — the technical handoff. It captures the expensive-to-rediscover knowledge:
- **Environment gotchas**: Lean 4.30.0 with **no Mathlib** (so no `norm_num`/`ring`/`set`/bare `le_refl`); `decide` needs `maxRecDepth 4000` and chokes on free variables; `set_option … in` must precede doc comments; parenthesize `by` inside `⟨…⟩`; `simp` collapses `x=x`→`True` (use `trivial`); the namespace `Hex0.`-qualification rule; the libcapstone shim.
- **The proof architecture as built** — all 56 proved declarations in dependency order, and the recipes that work (the per-instruction step pattern, `runFuel_add` chaining, the `let … + rfl + rw[←]` substitution idiom).
- **The full `core` instruction offset map** (every label, branch target, and the parse/store/comment/error paths).
- **The exact remaining lemmas** to close `loop_iteration`, with recommended order: `li_beq_eq` + spacing variants (quick win) → `storeByte_frame` (the one new technique) → byte → errors → comment → dispatch (~400–600 lines, mechanical reuse of proven patterns).
